</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-9d994bbd1e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:50:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Our data shows that this risky configuration is pretty common — among the networks that we observed using Microsoft DHCP server, &lt;b>57% have a DHCP server installed on a DC&lt;/b>. All these domains are vulnerable by default.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Although this risk was &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/troubleshoot/windows-server/networking/configure-dns-dynamic-updates-windows-server-2003#:~:text=When%20the%20DHCP%20Server%20service,computers%2C%20and%20by%20domain%20controllers.)\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>acknowledged by Microsoft&lt;/a> in their documentation, we believe that the awareness of this misconfiguration is not in accordance with its potential impact.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Our data shows that this risky configuration is pretty common — among the networks that we observed using Microsoft DHCP server, <b>57% have a DHCP server installed on a DC</b>. All these domains are vulnerable by default.</p>
<p>Although this risk was <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/troubleshoot/windows-server/networking/configure-dns-dynamic-updates-windows-server-2003#:~:text=When%20the%20DHCP%20Server%20service,computers%2C%20and%20by%20domain%20controllers.)" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">acknowledged by Microsoft</a> in their documentation, we believe that the awareness of this misconfiguration is not in accordance with its potential impact.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-75eef7d7e8&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:51:18Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>Mitigations for DHCP DNS attacks and how they can be bypassed&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>All the attacks described until now work with Microsoft DHCP servers’ default configuration. However, there are two settings that could help mitigate some of them. Let’s take a look at them, and see how they too can be bypassed.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>Mitigations for DHCP DNS attacks and how they can be bypassed</h2>
<p>All the attacks described until now work with Microsoft DHCP servers’ default configuration. However, there are two settings that could help mitigate some of them. Let’s take a look at them, and see how they too can be bypassed.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-72ad869a12&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:51:52Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>DHCP Name Protection&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>As we know, when a DHCP server creates a DNS record there&#39;s nothing stopping other clients from requesting the same FQDN and forcing the server to overwrite it. &lt;i>Name Protection&lt;/i> is a feature that&#39;s meant to prevent this from happening.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Name Protection is implemented using a special DNS record type — DHCID (DHCP client identifier). With Name Protection enabled, every time a DHCP server registers a record on behalf of a client, an additional DHCID record is created (Figure 21).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>DHCP Name Protection</h3>
<p>As we know, when a DHCP server creates a DNS record there's nothing stopping other clients from requesting the same FQDN and forcing the server to overwrite it. <i>Name Protection</i> is a feature that's meant to prevent this from happening.</p>
<p>Name Protection is implemented using a special DNS record type — DHCID (DHCP client identifier). With Name Protection enabled, every time a DHCP server registers a record on behalf of a client, an additional DHCID record is created (Figure 21).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="With Name Protection enabled, every time a DHCP server registers a record on behalf of a client, an additional DHCID record is created (Figure 21)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-59762140ea&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:53:20Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;With Name Protection enabled, every time a DHCP server registers a record on behalf of a client, an additional DHCID record is created (Figure 21).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;cff69efd-632b-45ac-ae25-343f2c553f08&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:53:10Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-21.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-21.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="With Name Protection enabled, every time a DHCP server registers a record on behalf of a client, an additional DHCID record is created (Figure 21)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 21: DHCID record created by a DHCP server with Name Protection enabled</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ad72f6a6ea&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:54:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>As you can see, the DHCID record value is a chunk of data encoded in Base64. This value (which we will analyze later in this post) is a unique signature meant to identify the DHCP client that requested the record creation or update.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When the DHCP server is requested to modify a DNS record, it calculates the client’s DHCID value and sends a DNS update that includes the updated data alongside that DHCID value.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If the record doesn&#39;t already exist on the DNS server, it simply creates the record and the matching DHCID record. However, if the Host (A) and DHCID records exist, the existing DHCID value is compared with the one sent by the DHCP server. The update is performed only if the values match.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>So, essentially, the DHCID record associates a DNS record with the client that created it. After this association is created, only this original client will be able to perform modifications to the record.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>As you can see, the DHCID record value is a chunk of data encoded in Base64. This value (which we will analyze later in this post) is a unique signature meant to identify the DHCP client that requested the record creation or update.</p>
<p>When the DHCP server is requested to modify a DNS record, it calculates the client’s DHCID value and sends a DNS update that includes the updated data alongside that DHCID value. </p>
<p>If the record doesn't already exist on the DNS server, it simply creates the record and the matching DHCID record. However, if the Host (A) and DHCID records exist, the existing DHCID value is compared with the one sent by the DHCP server. The update is performed only if the values match.</p>
<p>So, essentially, the DHCID record associates a DNS record with the client that created it. After this association is created, only this original client will be able to perform modifications to the record.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-4e8abd556c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:54:32Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h4>Bypassing Name Protection&lt;/h4>\r\n&lt;p>We found a way to bypass Name Protection by using a DHCP Release message — a message sent by DHCP clients to inform the server when they no longer need their leased IP address. To keep track of the addresses that it leased, the DHCP server maintains a table that stores the different addresses, their expiration times, and the unique identifier of the client who leased them (Figure 22).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h4>Bypassing Name Protection</h4>
<p>We found a way to bypass Name Protection by using a DHCP Release message — a message sent by DHCP clients to inform the server when they no longer need their leased IP address. To keep track of the addresses that it leased, the DHCP server maintains a table that stores the different addresses, their expiration times, and the unique identifier of the client who leased them (Figure 22).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="To keep track of the addresses that it leased, the DHCP server maintains a table that stores the different addresses, their expiration times, and the unique identifier of the client who leased them (Figure 22). " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-62a9beb65b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:58:54Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;To keep track of the addresses that it leased, the DHCP server maintains a table that stores the different addresses, their expiration times, and the unique identifier of the client who leased them (Figure 22).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;f5b8b90a-b00e-4fd9-ba40-46d733029d99&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:58:45Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-22.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-22.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="To keep track of the addresses that it leased, the DHCP server maintains a table that stores the different addresses, their expiration times, and the unique identifier of the client who leased them (Figure 22). "/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption"> Fig. 22: DHCP server lease table entry</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-c815fb8d30&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T17:59:56Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The unique identifier is simply the client’s MAC address. When receiving a Release message from a client, the DHCP server looks up an existing entry with a matching address and ID, and deletes it if it&#39;s found. When DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates are enabled, in addition to freeing the IP address, the DHCP server will also send a DNS Dynamic Update to delete the associated DNS record of the client.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If we can send a DHCP Release with a unique ID (MAC address) that matches our target’s ID, the DHCP server will delete the record, enabling us to register it for ourselves — &lt;b>the only requirement to bypass Name Protection is the victim’s MAC address!&lt;/b> (Note that there&#39;s no need to change our actual MAC — the value is taken from the DHCP header.)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If we’re on the same LAN as the target, finding its MAC is pretty trivial; for example, we can find it by sending an ARP request. But what if we’re not on the same LAN? We have another option.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The unique identifier is simply the client’s MAC address. When receiving a Release message from a client, the DHCP server looks up an existing entry with a matching address and ID, and deletes it if it's found. When DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates are enabled, in addition to freeing the IP address, the DHCP server will also send a DNS Dynamic Update to delete the associated DNS record of the client.</p>
<p>If we can send a DHCP Release with a unique ID (MAC address) that matches our target’s ID, the DHCP server will delete the record, enabling us to register it for ourselves — <b>the only requirement to bypass Name Protection is the victim’s MAC address!</b> (Note that there's no need to change our actual MAC — the value is taken from the DHCP header.)</p>
<p>If we’re on the same LAN as the target, finding its MAC is pretty trivial; for example, we can find it by sending an ARP request. But what if we’re not on the same LAN? We have another option.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1d7665ceb4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-06T21:24:34Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h4>Brute forcing DHCID records to bypass Name Protection&lt;/h4>\r\n&lt;p>DHCID records are defined in &lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4701.html\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>RFC 4701&lt;/a>, and their algorithm is pretty simple:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ol>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Concatenate the following values:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>DHCP HTYPE (hardware type). For Ethernet, the value is 01.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>DHCP Client ID option&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Record FQDN (&lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8484.html#:~:text=The%20same%20DNS,01%2000%2001\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>in DNS wire format&lt;/a>)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>SHA256 the result&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Add DHCID data bits (in the Windows implementation, this value is constant)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Encode the result in Base64&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ol>\r\n&lt;p>Figure 23 shows a DHCID calculation example.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h4>Brute forcing DHCID records to bypass Name Protection</h4>
<p>DHCID records are defined in <a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4701.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">RFC 4701</a>, and their algorithm is pretty simple:</p>
<ol>
<li><p>Concatenate the following values:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>DHCP HTYPE (hardware type). For Ethernet, the value is 01. </p>
</li>
<li><p>DHCP Client ID option</p>
</li>
<li><p>Record FQDN (<a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8484.html#:~:text=The%20same%20DNS,01%2000%2001" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">in DNS wire format</a>)</p>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p>SHA256 the result</p>
</li>
<li><p>Add DHCID data bits (in the Windows implementation, this value is constant)</p>
</li>
<li><p>Encode the result in Base64</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Figure 23 shows a DHCID calculation example.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Figure 23 shows a DHCID calculation example." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-5cdab8c5a9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:15:52Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Figure 23 shows a DHCID calculation example.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;5f50d2bb-784e-4ba5-a888-9e9f2ee8f6a4&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:15:44Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-23.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-23.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Figure 23 shows a DHCID calculation example."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption"> Fig. 23: A DHCID calculation example</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-4b7a07bfb4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:16:25Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Since we know the FQDN and the data bits are constant, the only variable is the client ID — which is again the client’s MAC address.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>DHCID records are normal DNS records, so any client can query the DNS server for their value. Because we know the algorithm to calculate a DHCID record, we can iterate all possible MAC addresses and compute their DHCID value and compare each result with our target record. When we get a match, we know we have found the correct MAC address. This allows attackers to brute force the MAC address in reasonable time — 248 possible MAC addresses could be cracked by a modern, dedicated computer in just a few days. We can reduce this time drastically if we only use common vendor IDs. An example of this process can be seen in Figure 24.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Since we know the FQDN and the data bits are constant, the only variable is the client ID — which is again the client’s MAC address.</p>
<p>DHCID records are normal DNS records, so any client can query the DNS server for their value. Because we know the algorithm to calculate a DHCID record, we can iterate all possible MAC addresses and compute their DHCID value and compare each result with our target record. When we get a match, we know we have found the correct MAC address. This allows attackers to brute force the MAC address in reasonable time — 248 possible MAC addresses could be cracked by a modern, dedicated computer in just a few days. We can reduce this time drastically if we only use common vendor IDs. An example of this process can be seen in Figure 24.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-51f74cf98d&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:17:51Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/akamai-security-research/blob/main/dhcp_dns_attacks/DHCID_calc.py\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>referenced code&lt;/a> can be used to calculate the DHCID value based on specified parameters.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The <a href="https://github.com/akamai/akamai-security-research/blob/main/dhcp_dns_attacks/DHCID_calc.py" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">referenced code</a> can be used to calculate the DHCID value based on specified parameters.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-5d16d96e30&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:18:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>The side-effect mitigations of Name Protection&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>DHCP Name Protection is meant for managed records: Essentially, the DHCP server protects records that were created by it from being modified by random clients. Name Protection doesn&#39;t have anything to do with client records.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Despite that, in some cases, Name Protection can still mitigate attacks on client records.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>When updating DNS records with Name Protection enabled, the DHCP server requires the presence of a DHCID record. Since normal DNS clients don&#39;t create DHCID records, client records are not accompanied by them. As a result, any attempt to update a client record from a DHCP server would fail (Figure 25).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>The side-effect mitigations of Name Protection</h3>
<p>DHCP Name Protection is meant for managed records: Essentially, the DHCP server protects records that were created by it from being modified by random clients. Name Protection doesn't have anything to do with client records.</p>
<p>Despite that, in some cases, Name Protection can still mitigate attacks on client records.</p>
<p>When updating DNS records with Name Protection enabled, the DHCP server requires the presence of a DHCID record. Since normal DNS clients don't create DHCID records, client records are not accompanied by them. As a result, any attempt to update a client record from a DHCP server would fail (Figure 25).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Any attempt to update a client record from a DHCP server would fail (Figure 25)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-e9f08973f6&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:21:06Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Any attempt to update a client record from a DHCP server would fail (Figure 25).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;995c40a3-6f74-4591-895f-155d40ff0aa3&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:20:58Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig25.png&#34;}}}">

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 25: DNS update failing when a DHCID record doesn&#39;t exist</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-dad23398df&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:19:40Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>This happens because of the way Name Protection is implemented. When a DHCP server with Name Protection enabled sends a DNS update, it adds a Prerequisites field to the request. This field specifies conditions that have to be met on the DNS server for the DNS update to take place. In Figure 26, we can see that the DNS update sent by the DHCP server includes a prerequisite for the DHCID value.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>This happens because of the way Name Protection is implemented. When a DHCP server with Name Protection enabled sends a DNS update, it adds a Prerequisites field to the request. This field specifies conditions that have to be met on the DNS server for the DNS update to take place. In Figure 26, we can see that the DNS update sent by the DHCP server includes a prerequisite for the DHCID value.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title=" In Figure 26, we can see that the DNS update sent by the DHCP server includes a prerequisite for the DHCID value." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-d60356ff1f&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:20:36Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;In Figure 26, we can see that the DNS update sent by the DHCP server includes a prerequisite for the DHCID value.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;a0f631c9-175c-4ca2-a19e-638dbf03c8f9&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:20:28Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-26.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-26.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt=" In Figure 26, we can see that the DNS update sent by the DHCP server includes a prerequisite for the DHCID value."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 26: DNS update prerequisites</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-01fef4a3ad&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:21:03Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>This means that the update would fail if a matching value doesn&#39;t exist. Since client records should never have a DHCID record, if Name Protection is enabled the client records should be protected from DHCP DNS overwrites without a way to bypass it. &lt;i>Should be&lt;/i>.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>This is not really part of the Name Protection feature — more a byproduct of it — as, by definition, Name Protection is meant to protect only managed records. Still, because of the logic we just described, it may also protect client records. But even this accidental defense can be bypassed.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>This means that the update would fail if a matching value doesn't exist. Since client records should never have a DHCID record, if Name Protection is enabled the client records should be protected from DHCP DNS overwrites without a way to bypass it. <i>Should be</i>.</p>
<p>This is not really part of the Name Protection feature — more a byproduct of it — as, by definition, Name Protection is meant to protect only managed records. Still, because of the logic we just described, it may also protect client records. But even this accidental defense can be bypassed.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-7834cdaa6b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:21:23Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h4>DHCP scopes to the rescue?&lt;/h4>\r\n&lt;p>DHCP servers support the ability to define multiple scopes — a scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease (Figure 27).&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h4>DHCP scopes to the rescue?</h4>
<p>DHCP servers support the ability to define multiple scopes — a scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease (Figure 27). </p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="container responsivegrid cmp-container--paddingLeftMedium cmp-container--paddingRightMedium aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    
    
    
   

    

          <div data-scroll-to-id="container-05cf8009f7" class="cmp-container ">
          
               <div class="image">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="DHCP servers support the ability to define multiple scopes — a scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease (Figure 27). " class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-4ef8f287f9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:22:48Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;DHCP servers support the ability to define multiple scopes — a scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease (Figure 27).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;6ee93051-1605-4988-b471-17eef497b8c7&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:22:38Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-27.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-27.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="DHCP servers support the ability to define multiple scopes — a scope is a defined set of IP addresses in a specific subnet that the DHCP can lease (Figure 27). "/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 27: An example of DHCP scopes </span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>

               
          </div>

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-76edbb32e5&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:23:48Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The separation into scopes allows a better management of address distribution, and also allows the application of different policies for different subnets. Name Protection is one of these policies, and it is enabled on the scope level, meaning that different scopes can have different configurations.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>As we mentioned earlier in this post, when we tried to perform a DHCP DNS overwrite on a client record, we failed because our lease was from a DHCP scope &lt;i>with&lt;/i> Name Protection. But there&#39;s an important thing to understand: Scope is a DHCP term. Client records are not aware of them and are not associated with any scope.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Because of that, if we can get a lease from another scope that has Name Protection disabled, we can “bypass” this mitigation. (How to get a lease from another scope that has Name Protection disabled is beyond the breadth of this post, but you can check out the &lt;a href=\&#34;https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/networking/technologies/dhcp/dhcp-subnet-options\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>DHCP relay option&lt;/a>)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>This means that even if a single scope on the server has Name Protection disabled, it should be enough for an attacker to overwrite client records (given one of the misconfigurations discussed earlier).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The separation into scopes allows a better management of address distribution, and also allows the application of different policies for different subnets. Name Protection is one of these policies, and it is enabled on the scope level, meaning that different scopes can have different configurations.</p>
<p>As we mentioned earlier in this post, when we tried to perform a DHCP DNS overwrite on a client record, we failed because our lease was from a DHCP scope <i>with</i> Name Protection. But there's an important thing to understand: Scope is a DHCP term. Client records are not aware of them and are not associated with any scope.</p>
<p>Because of that, if we can get a lease from another scope that has Name Protection disabled, we can “bypass” this mitigation. (How to get a lease from another scope that has Name Protection disabled is beyond the breadth of this post, but you can check out the <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/windows-server/networking/technologies/dhcp/dhcp-subnet-options" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">DHCP relay option</a>)</p>
<p>This means that even if a single scope on the server has Name Protection disabled, it should be enough for an attacker to overwrite client records (given one of the misconfigurations discussed earlier).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-ffa123cd59&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:25:14Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>DNS credential&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>Another setting that could be configured on the DHCP server is &lt;i>DNS credential&lt;/i>. This setting allows us to supply a domain user’s credential, and have it used by the DHCP server instead of the machine account when creating and updating records (Figure 28).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>DNS credential</h3>
<p>Another setting that could be configured on the DHCP server is <i>DNS credential</i>. This setting allows us to supply a domain user’s credential, and have it used by the DHCP server instead of the machine account when creating and updating records (Figure 28).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="container responsivegrid cmp-container--paddingLeftMedium cmp-container--paddingRightMedium aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    
    
    
   

    

          <div data-scroll-to-id="container-6bb210047c" class="cmp-container ">
          
               <div class="image">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="This setting allows us to supply a domain user’s credential, and have it used by the DHCP server instead of the machine account when creating and updating records (Figure 28)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-077f36018b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:26:30Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;This setting allows us to supply a domain user’s credential, and have it used by the DHCP server instead of the machine account when creating and updating records (Figure 28).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;549edd3b-32df-405e-8dd0-c7f6094ff630&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:26:21Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-28.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-28.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="This setting allows us to supply a domain user’s credential, and have it used by the DHCP server instead of the machine account when creating and updating records (Figure 28)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 28: DHCP DNS credential configuration</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>

               
          </div>

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-b697ced744&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:27:01Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Let&#39;s go back to the example in which a DHCP server was installed on a DC. Upon updating DNS records, the DC machine account was used, an account that has permissions over any record in the zone. With a DNS credential configured, a weak account could be used instead, and the attack would no longer work.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Configuring a DNS credential is very important, as it allows a reduction of the attack surface that the DHCP server exposes. It should be able to mitigate the most severe attacks we described earlier.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>However, there are two details you need to consider when using this feature:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The configured credential has to be a weak user. If we configure it as a domain admin, for example, the DHCP server would still be able to overwrite arbitrary records.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>DNS records created by the DHCP server would still be owned by the same credential, and would still be vulnerable to DHCP DNS overwrite.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Let's go back to the example in which a DHCP server was installed on a DC. Upon updating DNS records, the DC machine account was used, an account that has permissions over any record in the zone. With a DNS credential configured, a weak account could be used instead, and the attack would no longer work.</p>
<p>Configuring a DNS credential is very important, as it allows a reduction of the attack surface that the DHCP server exposes. It should be able to mitigate the most severe attacks we described earlier.</p>
<p>However, there are two details you need to consider when using this feature:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>The configured credential has to be a weak user. If we configure it as a domain admin, for example, the DHCP server would still be able to overwrite arbitrary records.</p>
</li>
<li><p>DNS records created by the DHCP server would still be owned by the same credential, and would still be vulnerable to DHCP DNS overwrite.</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-8e2c3c0be9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-06T21:14:54Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>DNSUpdateProxy group&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>During our investigation of Microsoft’s DHCP and its interaction with DNS, we found another feature that can be abused — the &lt;i>DNSUpdateProxy&lt;/i> group. This group is meant to solve two permission-related problems of managed Records: the upgraded client problem and the multiple DHCP server problem.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>DNSUpdateProxy group</h2>
<p>During our investigation of Microsoft’s DHCP and its interaction with DNS, we found another feature that can be abused — the <i>DNSUpdateProxy</i> group. This group is meant to solve two permission-related problems of managed Records: the upgraded client problem and the multiple DHCP server problem.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-fa7b5a6575&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:28:01Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>Upgraded client problem&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>Let’s consider the upgraded client problem first: A legacy client initially uses the DHCP server to register a DNS record, but is then upgraded to a newer OS that supports DNS Dynamic Updates. The client cannot modify its record directly, as the record is owned by the DHCP server that created it.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>To solve this problem, the DHCP server can be added to the DNSUpdateProxy group.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>This group has two effects: First, when its members create a DNS record, the record’s ACL is different from normal managed records — &lt;i>the Authenticated Users&lt;/i> group is given write permission over the record. This means that any client in the domain can modify it (Figure 29).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>Upgraded client problem</h3>
<p>Let’s consider the upgraded client problem first: A legacy client initially uses the DHCP server to register a DNS record, but is then upgraded to a newer OS that supports DNS Dynamic Updates. The client cannot modify its record directly, as the record is owned by the DHCP server that created it.</p>
<p>To solve this problem, the DHCP server can be added to the DNSUpdateProxy group.</p>
<p>This group has two effects: First, when its members create a DNS record, the record’s ACL is different from normal managed records — <i>the Authenticated Users</i> group is given write permission over the record. This means that any client in the domain can modify it (Figure 29).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="container responsivegrid cmp-container--paddingLeftMedium cmp-container--paddingRightMedium aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    
    
    
   

    

          <div data-scroll-to-id="container-eb709147af" class="cmp-container ">
          
               <div class="image">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="First, when its members create a DNS record, the record’s ACL is different from normal managed records — the Authenticated Users group is given write permission over the record. This means that any client in the domain can modify it (Figure 29)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-e4cbc36727&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:30:59Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;First, when its members create a DNS record, the record’s ACL is different from normal managed records — the Authenticated Users group is given write permission over the record. This means that any client in the domain can modify it (Figure 29).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;afa34c82-be19-4ba3-a00a-1855525ce808&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:30:51Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-29.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-29.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="First, when its members create a DNS record, the record’s ACL is different from normal managed records — the Authenticated Users group is given write permission over the record. This means that any client in the domain can modify it (Figure 29)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 29: DNSUpdateProxy record ACL</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>

               
          </div>

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-96da29e2d4&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T18:59:47Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The second effect is a “record takeover” feature — the first client that modifies a record that was created by a DNSUpdateProxy member is granted ownership over it, and removes the authenticated users’ write permission. This solves the upgraded client problem by allowing clients to modify and take over their own record once they are required to do so.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The second effect is a “record takeover” feature — the first client that modifies a record that was created by a DNSUpdateProxy member is granted ownership over it, and removes the authenticated users’ write permission. This solves the upgraded client problem by allowing clients to modify and take over their own record once they are required to do so.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-48db1bff04&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:32:29Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>Multiple DHCP server problem&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>The second problem arises when multiple DHCP servers are required to work together. In this example we have two DHCP servers — &lt;i>DHCP1&lt;/i> and &lt;i>DHCP2&lt;/i>, and a client PC1 registers a DNS record through DHCP1.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>Multiple DHCP server problem</h3>
<p>The second problem arises when multiple DHCP servers are required to work together. In this example we have two DHCP servers — <i>DHCP1</i> and <i>DHCP2</i>, and a client PC1 registers a DNS record through DHCP1.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-c451bf4648&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:25:52Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>Now, let&#39;s imagine that DHCP1 goes offline for some reason, and DHCP2 is brought into action. The client’s lease expires, so it contacts DHCP2 for a new one. When DHCP2 leases the new IP and tries to modify the DNS record for the client, it fails — because the record is owned by DHCP1 (Figure 30).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>Now, let's imagine that DHCP1 goes offline for some reason, and DHCP2 is brought into action. The client’s lease expires, so it contacts DHCP2 for a new one. When DHCP2 leases the new IP and tries to modify the DNS record for the client, it fails — because the record is owned by DHCP1 (Figure 30).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="The second problem arises when multiple DHCP servers are required to work together. In this example we have two DHCP servers — DHCP1 and DHCP2, and a client PC1 registers a DNS record through DHCP1" class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-90fda7dd36&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:24:25Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;The second problem arises when multiple DHCP servers are required to work together. In this example we have two DHCP servers — DHCP1 and DHCP2, and a client PC1 registers a DNS record through DHCP1&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;fcf5c867-7a68-4e41-91d3-63b652919475&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:22:49Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig30.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig30.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="The second problem arises when multiple DHCP servers are required to work together. In this example we have two DHCP servers — DHCP1 and DHCP2, and a client PC1 registers a DNS record through DHCP1"/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 30: An example of a multiple DHCP server setup</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-417a47620b&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:07:19Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>This problem can again be solved by using DNSUpdateProxy, because of an additional feature of this group. If a member of DNSUpdateProxy tries to modify a record that’s owned by another member, the update is successful because of the ACL, &lt;b>but this time the ACL and ownership don’t change.&lt;/b> This allows multiple servers to “co-own” records.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>This problem can again be solved by using DNSUpdateProxy, because of an additional feature of this group. If a member of DNSUpdateProxy tries to modify a record that’s owned by another member, the update is successful because of the ACL, <b>but this time the ACL and ownership don’t change.</b> This allows multiple servers to “co-own” records.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-235beda4a1&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:26:21Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>A security risk and a bug&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>By now you probably understand that the DNSUpdateProxy group exposes a security risk:&amp;nbsp; Any record that was created by members of this group could be “stolen” by any authenticated user. This is not a vulnerability, it&#39;s just an abuse of the feature’s design. This risk is acknowledged by Microsoft.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>In addition to this risk, we identified another problem that stems from what seems to be a bug in the DNSUpdateProxy feature implementation. When a member of the group creates &lt;b>its own&lt;/b> DNS record, it&#39;s created with the same vulnerable ACL, for which authenticated users have write permissions.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Figure 31 shows an example. Our DHCP server &lt;i>dhcp1.aka.test&lt;/i> record initially has a secure ACL.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>A security risk and a bug</h3>
<p>By now you probably understand that the DNSUpdateProxy group exposes a security risk:  Any record that was created by members of this group could be “stolen” by any authenticated user. This is not a vulnerability, it's just an abuse of the feature’s design. This risk is acknowledged by Microsoft.</p>
<p>In addition to this risk, we identified another problem that stems from what seems to be a bug in the DNSUpdateProxy feature implementation. When a member of the group creates <b>its own</b> DNS record, it's created with the same vulnerable ACL, for which authenticated users have write permissions.</p>
<p>Figure 31 shows an example. Our DHCP server <i>dhcp1.aka.test</i> record initially has a secure ACL.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="container responsivegrid cmp-container--paddingLeftMedium cmp-container--paddingRightMedium aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    
    
    
   

    

          <div data-scroll-to-id="container-0bc99f5fa8" class="cmp-container ">
          
               <div class="image">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="Figure 31 shows an example. Our DHCP server dhcp1.aka.test record initially has a secure ACL." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-3cd5ce4aaf&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:33:56Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;Figure 31 shows an example. Our DHCP server dhcp1.aka.test record initially has a secure ACL.&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;9d6d61b4-a082-4ccd-844e-4a5972643d91&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:33:48Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-32.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-32.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="Figure 31 shows an example. Our DHCP server dhcp1.aka.test record initially has a secure ACL."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 31: DHCP server initial ACL</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>

               
          </div>

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-29cf5792fc&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:34:10Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>We can see that the machine account has permissions over it, and the Authenticated Users group is nowhere to be found. Now, we add the server to the DNSUpdateProxy group and trigger a recreation of the DNS record. This can happen for several reasons; for example, if the server name is changed. After the DNS record is recreated, we inspect its new ACL (Figure 32).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>We can see that the machine account has permissions over it, and the Authenticated Users group is nowhere to be found. Now, we add the server to the DNSUpdateProxy group and trigger a recreation of the DNS record. This can happen for several reasons; for example, if the server name is changed. After the DNS record is recreated, we inspect its new ACL (Figure 32).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="container responsivegrid cmp-container--paddingLeftMedium cmp-container--paddingRightMedium aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">

    
    
    
   

    

          <div data-scroll-to-id="container-9f8f40d9d7" class="cmp-container ">
          
               <div class="image">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="This can happen for several reasons; for example, if the server name is changed. After the DNS record is recreated, we inspect its new ACL (Figure 32)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-93e019f078&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:34:38Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;This can happen for several reasons; for example, if the server name is changed. After the DNS record is recreated, we inspect its new ACL (Figure 32).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;dc94bf85-1552-4abc-abf2-cc1033278a31&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:34:29Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-33.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-33.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="This can happen for several reasons; for example, if the server name is changed. After the DNS record is recreated, we inspect its new ACL (Figure 32)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 32: DHCP server vulnerable ACL</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>

               
          </div>

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-22c0614802&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:32:41Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>We see that the new DNS record is now writable by domain users. This is obviously not an intended part of the feature — managed records created by the server are meant to have a modified ACL, but the server’s own client record shouldn’t be affected.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>We see that the new DNS record is now writable by domain users. This is obviously not an intended part of the feature — managed records created by the server are meant to have a modified ACL, but the server’s own client record shouldn’t be affected.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" id="mitigation" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;mitigation&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T20:14:22Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>Mitigating DHCP DNS attacks&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>There are many risks relating to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates. Let&#39;s summarize all the different possible server configurations and learn how to mitigate the attacks we just described.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We will refer to the two types of records — managed records that were created by the DHCP server, and client records that were created by Windows clients directly.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>The TL;DR version is:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Disable DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates if you don&#39;t need them&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Client records should be safe if you configure a weak user as the DNS credential&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Managed records can’t be protected from spoofing with any configuration; use static DNS records for sensitive non-Windows hosts, if possible&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Do not use DNSUpdateProxy; use the same DNS credential across all your DHCP servers instead&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>Mitigating DHCP DNS attacks</h2>
<p>There are many risks relating to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates. Let's summarize all the different possible server configurations and learn how to mitigate the attacks we just described.</p>
<p>We will refer to the two types of records — managed records that were created by the DHCP server, and client records that were created by Windows clients directly.</p>
<p>The TL;DR version is:</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Disable DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates if you don't need them</p>
</li>
<li><p>Client records should be safe if you configure a weak user as the DNS credential</p>
</li>
<li><p>Managed records can’t be protected from spoofing with any configuration; use static DNS records for sensitive non-Windows hosts, if possible</p>
</li>
<li><p>Do not use DNSUpdateProxy; use the same DNS credential across all your DHCP servers instead</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-1f0d88f937&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:34:44Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>DNS credential&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>This is the best way to mitigate DHCP DNS overwrites on client records. Configure a weak user with a strong password that is dedicated for this purpose. &lt;b>If you run a DHCP server on your DC, this is critical. &lt;/b>This setting is not going to stop DHCP DNS overwrites on managed records.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>DNS credential</h3>
<p>This is the best way to mitigate DHCP DNS overwrites on client records. Configure a weak user with a strong password that is dedicated for this purpose. <b>If you run a DHCP server on your DC, this is critical. </b>This setting is not going to stop DHCP DNS overwrites on managed records.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-061d5ed1c3&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:36:06Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>Name Protection&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>Name Protection should in theory protect managed records, but in practice attackers can bypass it pretty easily. It should still be enabled to make overwrites less trivial.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Although Name Protection is not meant to protect client records, if it&#39;s enabled on all the scopes on the server, overwrite attacks would still be mitigated.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;a href=\&#34;https://www.zubairalexander.com/blog/configuring-name-protection-on-a-dhcp-server-to-prevent-name-squatting/#:~:text=To%20configure%20Name%20Protection%20at,then%20click%20the%20DNS%20tab.\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>When configuring Name Protection on Microsoft DHCP,&lt;/a> there are two ways to apply it: at the server level or at the scope level. One might think that Name Protection being enabled on the server level would mean that Name protection would be enabled on the server level, right? Well, that&#39;s not actually the case. Enabling Name Protection on the server level only makes sure that &lt;b>new&lt;/b> scopes on the server are created with the setting enabled, but it doesn’t enable it on existing scopes. It&#39;s important to verify that Name Protection is enabled on the scope level of each of the scopes on the server.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>Name Protection</h3>
<p>Name Protection should in theory protect managed records, but in practice attackers can bypass it pretty easily. It should still be enabled to make overwrites less trivial.</p>
<p>Although Name Protection is not meant to protect client records, if it's enabled on all the scopes on the server, overwrite attacks would still be mitigated.</p>
<p><a href="https://www.zubairalexander.com/blog/configuring-name-protection-on-a-dhcp-server-to-prevent-name-squatting/#:~:text=To%20configure%20Name%20Protection%20at,then%20click%20the%20DNS%20tab." target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">When configuring Name Protection on Microsoft DHCP,</a> there are two ways to apply it: at the server level or at the scope level. One might think that Name Protection being enabled on the server level would mean that Name protection would be enabled on the server level, right? Well, that's not actually the case. Enabling Name Protection on the server level only makes sure that <b>new</b> scopes on the server are created with the setting enabled, but it doesn’t enable it on existing scopes. It's important to verify that Name Protection is enabled on the scope level of each of the scopes on the server.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-b3c51e833e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:37:09Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>DNSUpdateProxy&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>You should not use this group. It&#39;s a security risk because all the records created by its members are susceptible to overwrites.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If you have multiple DHCP servers and you want them to work together you should use DNS credential instead. Simply configure the same DNS credential on all the DHCP servers — this will allow them to edit one another&#39;s records.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>DNSUpdateProxy is only useful if you have Windows NT 4.0 clients (or older) that you plan to upgrade soon. And if you have anything of that vintage, you&#39;ve got bigger problems than DNSUpdateProxy.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>If, for some reason, you are required to use DNSUpdateProxy, it’s recommended that you create a static DNS record for each of the group members. A static record would be owned by its creating account, which should be different from the different servers&#39; machine accounts. This will prevent servers from creating their own records with insecure permissions.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>DNSUpdateProxy</h3>
<p>You should not use this group. It's a security risk because all the records created by its members are susceptible to overwrites.</p>
<p>If you have multiple DHCP servers and you want them to work together you should use DNS credential instead. Simply configure the same DNS credential on all the DHCP servers — this will allow them to edit one another's records.</p>
<p>DNSUpdateProxy is only useful if you have Windows NT 4.0 clients (or older) that you plan to upgrade soon. And if you have anything of that vintage, you've got bigger problems than DNSUpdateProxy.</p>
<p>If, for some reason, you are required to use DNSUpdateProxy, it’s recommended that you create a static DNS record for each of the group members. A static record would be owned by its creating account, which should be different from the different servers' machine accounts. This will prevent servers from creating their own records with insecure permissions.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-0f9103fe0c&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:37:28Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h3>DHCP DNS spoofing&lt;/h3>\r\n&lt;p>There is no way to stop unauthenticated attackers from creating nonexisting DNS records. The only way to do this would be to disable DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates on all DHCP servers. In general, if the DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates feature is not required in your environment, disabling them is probably a good idea. This will eliminate some risks and will help reduce the attack surface.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h3>DHCP DNS spoofing</h3>
<p>There is no way to stop unauthenticated attackers from creating nonexisting DNS records. The only way to do this would be to disable DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates on all DHCP servers. In general, if the DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates feature is not required in your environment, disabling them is probably a good idea. This will eliminate some risks and will help reduce the attack surface.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" id="detecting" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;detecting&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:35:18Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>Detecting misconfigurations with Invoke-DHCPCheckup&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>To help you traverse the mess of possible DHCP configurations, we are releasing a PowerShell tool called &lt;a href=\&#34;https://github.com/akamai/Invoke-DHCPCheckup\&#34; target=\&#34;_blank\&#34; rel=\&#34;nofollow noreferrer\&#34;>Invoke-DHCPCheckup&lt;/a> to identify risks related to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 33).&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>Detecting misconfigurations with Invoke-DHCPCheckup</h2>
<p>To help you traverse the mess of possible DHCP configurations, we are releasing a PowerShell tool called <a href="https://github.com/akamai/Invoke-DHCPCheckup" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noreferrer">Invoke-DHCPCheckup</a> to identify risks related to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 33).</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="image aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div class="cmp-image__wrapper    ">
  <div data-cmp-lazy data-title="To help you traverse the mess of possible DHCP configurations, we are releasing a PowerShell tool called Invoke-DHCPCheckup to identify risks related to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 33)." class="cmp-image " itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;image-7385d7d292&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/image&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-12T13:21:04Z&#34;,&#34;dc:title&#34;:&#34;To help you traverse the mess of possible DHCP configurations, we are releasing a PowerShell tool called Invoke-DHCPCheckup to identify risks related to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 33).&#34;,&#34;image&#34;:{&#34;repo:id&#34;:&#34;e442290e-4214-4e6e-8361-cc49c278e1a5&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-07T16:35:43Z&#34;,&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;image/png&#34;,&#34;repo:path&#34;:&#34;/content/dam/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-34.png&#34;}}}">
    
      
        
          <img src="/site/en/images/blog/2023/spoofing-dns-by-abusing-dhcp-fig-34.png" loading="lazy" class="cmp-image__image" itemprop="contentUrl" data-cmp-hook-image="image" alt="To help you traverse the mess of possible DHCP configurations, we are releasing a PowerShell tool called Invoke-DHCPCheckup to identify risks related to DHCP DNS Dynamic Updates (Figure 33)."/>
        
        
      
    
    

    <span class="cmp-image__title" itemprop="caption">Fig. 33: Invoke-DHCPCheckup example output</span>
    
    
  </div>
</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pt-none aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-0fc351282e&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-05T19:39:43Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;p>The tool identifies the following misconfigurations:&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>DNS credential&lt;/b>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>DNS credential is not configured&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>The configured DNS credential is of a strong user&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>Name Protection&lt;/b>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Name Protection is not enabled on a scope&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Name Protection is not enabled by default on new scopes&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>DNSUpdateProxy&lt;/b>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Display group members&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>Specify whether the members are DHCP servers&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;p>&lt;b>Weak record ACLs&lt;/b>&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;ul>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>List records owned by DHCP servers (managed records)&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;li>&lt;p>List records that could be overwritten by authenticated users&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;/li>\r\n&lt;/ul>\r\n&lt;p>This tool relies on DHCP server management API and requires a strong user to run, therefore&amp;nbsp; the tool is mainly meant for blue teams.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <p>The tool identifies the following misconfigurations:</p>
<p><b>DNS credential</b></p>
<ul>
<li><p>DNS credential is not configured</p>
</li>
<li><p>The configured DNS credential is of a strong user</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Name Protection</b></p>
<ul>
<li><p>Name Protection is not enabled on a scope</p>
</li>
<li><p>Name Protection is not enabled by default on new scopes</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><b>DNSUpdateProxy</b></p>
<ul>
<li><p>Display group members </p>
</li>
<li><p>Specify whether the members are DHCP servers</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Weak record ACLs</b></p>
<ul>
<li><p>List records owned by DHCP servers (managed records)</p>
</li>
<li><p>List records that could be overwritten by authenticated users</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This tool relies on DHCP server management API and requires a strong user to run, therefore  the tool is mainly meant for blue teams.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-f5bfadcc07&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-06T22:40:02Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>Summary&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>We reported all our findings to Microsoft, which responded that all the above-mentioned problems are either by design, or not severe enough to receive a fix.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>We tend to disagree. The impact of the attacks that we highlighted can be very significant — the ability to overwrite DNS records without any authentication enables attackers to gain a machine-in-the-middle position on hosts in the domain. This could easily expose sensitive information and credentials, and could also enable relay attacks, allowing attackers to breach AD domains and escalate privileges. The statistics we shared in this post demonstrate how solid the threat is for many data center networks.&lt;/p>\r\n&lt;p>Since a fix for these problems is not planned, we urge defenders to scan their environments using Invoke-DHCPCheckup to try to locate the risky misconfigurations that we’ve highlighted. Spoiler alert — if you didn’t change the default configuration, you are vulnerable.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>Summary</h2>
<p>We reported all our findings to Microsoft, which responded that all the above-mentioned problems are either by design, or not severe enough to receive a fix.</p>
<p>We tend to disagree. The impact of the attacks that we highlighted can be very significant — the ability to overwrite DNS records without any authentication enables attackers to gain a machine-in-the-middle position on hosts in the domain. This could easily expose sensitive information and credentials, and could also enable relay attacks, allowing attackers to breach AD domains and escalate privileges. The statistics we shared in this post demonstrate how solid the threat is for many data center networks.</p>
<p>Since a fix for these problems is not planned, we urge defenders to scan their environments using Invoke-DHCPCheckup to try to locate the risky misconfigurations that we’ve highlighted. Spoiler alert — if you didn’t change the default configuration, you are vulnerable.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
<div class="text text__pb-20 aem-GridColumn aem-GridColumn--default--12">
<div data-cmp-is="text" class="cmp-text" data-cmp-data-layer="{&#34;text-04a55208c9&#34;:{&#34;@type&#34;:&#34;akamai/components/text&#34;,&#34;repo:modifyDate&#34;:&#34;2023-12-06T21:16:08Z&#34;,&#34;xdm:text&#34;:&#34;&lt;h2>Stay tuned&lt;/h2>\r\n&lt;p>In an upcoming blog post, we will release &lt;i>DDSpoof&lt;/i> (DHCP DNS Spoof) — a tool that implements all the attacks that we described in this article. We will show how unauthenticated attackers can collect necessary data from DHCP servers, identify vulnerable DNS records, overwrite them, and use that ability to compromise AD domains.&lt;/p>\r\n&#34;}}">
    <h2>Stay tuned</h2>
<p>In an upcoming blog post, we will release <i>DDSpoof</i> (DHCP DNS Spoof) — a tool that implements all the attacks that we described in this article. We will show how unauthenticated attackers can collect necessary data from DHCP servers, identify vulnerable DNS records, overwrite them, and use that ability to compromise AD domains.</p>

</div>

    

</div>
